style="background-color: #eee"><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><div style="text-align: left;">Source: Bulgarian <a href="/wiki/Aeronautical_Information_Publication" title="Aeronautical Information Publication">AIP</a> at <a href="/wiki/European_Organisation_for_the_Safety_of_Air_Navigation" class="mw-redirect" title="European Organisation for the Safety of Air Navigation">EUROCONTROL</a><sup id="cite_ref-AIP_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AIP-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Sofia Airport</b> (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>SOF</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>LBSF</b>) (<a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">Bulgarian</a>: <span lang="bg">\xd0\x9b\xd0\xb5\xd1\x82\xd0\xb8\xd1\x89\xd0\xb5 \xd0\xa1\xd0\xbe\xd1\x84\xd0\xb8\xd1\x8f, Letishte Sofiya</span>) is the main <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>, located 10&#160;km (6.2&#160;mi) east<sup id="cite_ref-AIP_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AIP-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> of the centre of the capital <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a>. In 2019 the airport surpassed 7 million passengers for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The airport serves as the home base for <a href="/wiki/BH_Air" title="BH Air">BH Air</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria_Air" title="Bulgaria Air">Bulgaria Air</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Air_Charter" title="Bulgarian Air Charter">Bulgarian Air Charter</a> and as a base for both <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wizz_Air" title="Wizz Air">Wizz Air</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Vrazhdebna_Air_Base" title="Vrazhdebna Air Base">Vrazhdebna Air Base</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Air_Force" title="Bulgarian Air Force">Bulgarian Air Force</a> is at the airport. \n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toctext">Cargo</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Statistics"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Statistics</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Traffic"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Traffic</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">Early years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 16 September 1937, <a href="/wiki/Boris_III_of_Bulgaria" title="Boris III of Bulgaria">Tsar Boris III</a> signed a <a href="/wiki/Decree" title="Decree">decree</a> which declared land within the Village of Vrazhdebna be allocated for the construction of an airport. Construction then began on the site, which was 11&#160;km (6.8&#160;mi) from the city centre. Two years later in 1939, Sofia Airport opened its first passenger waiting room, and after another two years was followed by a fully constructed airfield with a fully paved runway.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>From June through September 1938, Yugoslav airline <a href="/wiki/Aeroput" title="Aeroput">Aeroput</a> connected Sofia with Belgrade thrice weekly using <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Model_10_Electra" title="Lockheed Model 10 Electra">Lockheed Model 10 Electra</a> planes.<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, the facilities were used by the military. Mail, perishable freight and passenger operations began in 1947 from buildings on the north side of the airport. The passenger terminal (now Terminal 1) on the south side was completed during the Second World War in the manner of a then-modern European railway terminus to designs by the architect Ivan Marangozov. It opened after several years of delay in 1947. The structure comprised a government wing to the west, an international handling area in the middle, and a domestic handling area to the east. At that time, it was planned that the airport would eventually have two intersecting runways at a 30-degree angle to each other.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The terminal had substantially reached its capacity of some 600,000 passengers a year by the later 1960s and was subjected to a number of refurbishments and extensions beginning in the spring of 1968. In 1975, a new international arrivals handling extension was opened to the west of the building, the domestic area to the east was enlarged, the government handling area was removed to a dedicated terminal some distance to the west, a <a href="/wiki/Very_Important_Person" class="mw-redirect" title="Very Important Person">VIP</a> handling area opened in the old terminal, apron area was extended to the east and new taxiways opened. A <a href="/wiki/Bonded_warehouse" title="Bonded warehouse">bonded warehouse</a> opened to the east of the terminal square in 1969 and several new hangars followed to the east of the first maintenance base in the 1970s. A new checked <a href="/wiki/Baggage_handling_system" title="Baggage handling system">baggage handling system</a> opened to the north of the building in the early 1980s, cosmetic and traffic reorganising refurbishments were carried out in 1990, with a substantial landside extension following in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-europa.eu_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-europa.eu-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By the late 1970s, the terminal was handling in the region of three million passengers a year, a million of them on domestic routes. Passenger numbers fell off sharply after the 1979 CMEA ("Comecon") oil price shock and recovered to just over a million a year by the late 1980s. In the early and mid-1990s, domestic traffic practically ceased, while foreign traffic reduced significantly. The latter began growing apace in the late 1990s and early 2000s to reach its current levels. The terminal was last refurbished partially in 1990. In 2000, it underwent a wholesale update in which the international arrivals area was moved to the east wing where domestic handling had been, the former international arrivals area to the west was closed, and the layout of the central international departures area was changed in line with world developments. Despite the work to the old terminal, the airport was becoming overwhelmed with passenger traffic.<sup id="cite_ref-europa.eu_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-europa.eu-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Options for different airport developments began to be examined in the mid-1960s. One option was to relocate the facility to a new site, with some locations up to 70&#160;km (43&#160;mi) from Sofia.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Another option involved extending the airport\'s area radically to the north-east and gradually removing the focus of the airport there. A third option was to develop substantially the same site. By the later 1980s, the authorities had settled on the last option.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development_since_the_1990s">Development since the 1990s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Development since the 1990s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Project design, involving a new terminal to the east of the old facility, a new runway to the north of (and parallel to) the existing runway, and taxiways, was completed by the mid-1990s. A finance package involving very significant European and Kuwaiti investment was initially agreed in 1998 and was in place by 2000. Work began in 2001. The new runway and some taxiways were completed in mid-2006. Terminal 2 was formally inaugurated on 27 December 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-europa.eu_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-europa.eu-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Design and construction of a new control tower was discussed in 2006 but this project appeared to be in abeyance by 2008. Over the years, Sofia Airport has been criticised for its lack of world class air freight facilities and for some access problems. Passengers to and from the Bulgarian interior have to access or egress the airport through crowded rail and coach facilities in central Sofia. A rail link has been discussed on several occasions since the 1960s. The next best thing, perhaps, was the extension of <a href="/wiki/Sofia_Metro" title="Sofia Metro">Sofia Metro</a> Line 1 some 5&#160;km from Blvd <a href="/wiki/Tsarigradsko_shose" title="Tsarigradsko shose">Tsarigradsko shose</a>. This was opened on 2 April 2015 under the name <a href="/wiki/Sofia_Airport_Metro_Station" title="Sofia Airport Metro Station">Sofia Airport Metro Station</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-railwaygazette.com_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-railwaygazette.com-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The airport metro station is adjacent to Terminal 2.  Connection with terminal 1 is by free shuttle bus.\n</p><p>The airport is occasionally criticised as a source of environmental noise and pollution and strict noise abatement procedures have been enforced for departing traffic since the mid-1970s, while arriving traffic is generally routed to approach the field from the east, clear of <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-europa.eu_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-europa.eu-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A significant and recurring operational criticism of Sofia Airport has concerned its historical lack of all-weather operations capability. Though the new runway was designed for ICAO Category 3 operations, in 2007 it emerged that radio interference from security fencing, and most significantly from a large newly built lorry park, prevented certification (and hence use) of the associated radio navigational aids. During the winter months, the airport, located on a high alluvial plain surrounded by mountains, suffers from very significant and frequent fog precipitation. In such circumstances, flights are redirected to diversion airports in Bulgaria or neighbouring countries, lengthening journeys by many hours.<sup id="cite_ref-europa.eu_7-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-europa.eu-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 3 June 2016, the Bulgarian government launched a tender for the operation of Sofia Airport.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Expected to bring in 1.2 billion lev (600 million euro) to the state over 35 years, the tender has reportedly attracted interest from the operators of airports in <a href="/wiki/Munich_Airport" title="Munich Airport">Munich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zurich_Airport" title="Zurich Airport">Zurich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lyon_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Lyon Airport">Lyon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Airport" title="Dublin Airport">Dublin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">London-Heathrow</a> and as well as other operators.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of 22 July 2020, the concessionaire of Sofia Airport is the Sof Connect consortium, consisting of the French investment fund Meridiam (99% stake) and Austria\'s Strabag (1% stake). The concession period runs for 35 years. The airport\'s operator for the first 12 years of the concession period will be Munich Airport International.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> On 20 April 2021 SOF Connect AD officially have became the concessionaire of the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airport_reconstruction">Airport reconstruction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Airport reconstruction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sofia_Airport_model.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Sofia_Airport_model.jpg/220px-Sofia_Airport_model.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Sofia_Airport_model.jpg/330px-Sofia_Airport_model.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Sofia_Airport_model.jpg/440px-Sofia_Airport_model.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sofia_Airport_model.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A model of the new airport terminal in the departures hall</div></div></div>\n<p>As a result of growing air traffic and passenger numbers, the airport facilities struggled to cope despite several expansions in the years prior. Planning began in the 1990s for a new terminal to be constructed at the airport. The new runway was offset from the old by 210&#160;m (690&#160;ft) with the eastern end crossing the Iskar River bed on a specially constructed bridge. New taxiways were also constructed, allowing for 22 aircraft movements per hour. The old runway was then to be used as a taxiway only.<sup id="cite_ref-concession-sof.bg_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-concession-sof.bg-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The new runway and taxiways were opened in mid-2006, and Terminal 2 formally opened in late 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-europa.eu_7-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-europa.eu-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Total cost of the project was planned at 200 million <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euros</a>. Finance was secured in 1997\xe2\x80\x9398 from the <a href="/wiki/European_Investment_Bank" title="European Investment Bank">European Investment Bank</a> (60 million euro), <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Fund_for_Arab_Economic_Development" title="Kuwait Fund for Arab Economic Development">Kuwait Fund for Arab Economic Development</a> (12.3 million <a href="/wiki/Kuwaiti_dinar" title="Kuwaiti dinar">Kuwaiti dinars</a>, approximately 41.5 million euro), and the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> <a href="/wiki/PHARE" class="mw-redirect" title="PHARE">PHARE</a> Programme (7.6 million euro). In August 2000, an <a href="/wiki/Instrument_for_Structural_Policies_for_Pre-Accession" title="Instrument for Structural Policies for Pre-Accession">ISPA</a> grant of 50 million euro was allocated and in December the financing memorandum was signed.<sup id="cite_ref-europa.eu_7-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-europa.eu-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The construction works were in two lots: the new terminal with its surrounding infrastructure and the new runway. The first lot was allocated to the German branch of Austrian company <a href="/wiki/Strabag" title="Strabag">Strabag</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> while the second was won by a consortium of Kuwaiti company Mohamed Abdulmohsin al-Kharafi &amp; Sons and UAE-based Admak General Contracting Company.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The initial completion deadline for the new terminal was 15 December 2004 to a total budget of 112.2 million euro. Immediately after work started, Strabag contested the geological surveys by Dutch consultants NACO B.V. and demanded additional funding for unexpected additional works. The delay was ten months, and construction resumed after the Bulgarian government agreed to augment the project\'s value by 4.8 million euro and extend the deadline to 31 August 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2004 Strabag demanded an additional 6 million euro due to rising steel prices.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The Ministry of Transportation rejected the claim, backed by a report from NACO. In May 2005, the contractor threatened to take the case to international arbitration.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> In August 2005, it became clear that Strabag would not be able to meet the changed deadline, slippage being put at six to eight weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> In November 2005, Strabag asked for eight months\' further extension.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Runway_system">Runway system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Runway system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 31 August 2006, Sofia Airport put its new runway system into operation, replacing the old and out-of-date facilities. The new runway is offset 210&#160;m (690&#160;ft) to the north of the old runway, with the eastern end of its 3,600&#160;m (11,811&#160;ft) long strip crossing over the Iskar river bed on a specially constructed bridge. New rapid and connecting taxiways were built to open way for 20 aircraft movements per hour at a high level of safety. The navigational aids installed on the new runway enable landing operations under low visibility conditions at category IIIB of the ICAO standards.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Two de-icing platforms were constructed to allow centralised de-icing procedures in winter. They are one element in the overall strategy of Sofia Airport for environmental protection and reduction of the harmful effects resulting from the airport operations. At the moment there is another de-icing platform under construction.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (January 2019)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Control_tower">Control tower</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Control tower">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SOFIA_NEW_TOWER_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/SOFIA_NEW_TOWER_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-SOFIA_NEW_TOWER_-_panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/SOFIA_NEW_TOWER_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-SOFIA_NEW_TOWER_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/SOFIA_NEW_TOWER_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-SOFIA_NEW_TOWER_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="4352" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SOFIA_NEW_TOWER_-_panoramio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 2012 Air Traffic Control Tower (U/C).</div></div></div>\n<p>A new 50&#160;m (160&#160;ft)<sup id="cite_ref-concession-sof.bg_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-concession-sof.bg-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> control tower was inaugurated officially on 5 December 2012 by the PM <a href="/wiki/Boyko_Borisov" title="Boyko Borisov">Boyko Borisov</a> and the minister of transport <a href="/wiki/Ivaylo_Moskovski" title="Ivaylo Moskovski">Ivaylo Moskovski</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The tower was built by Glavbolgarstroy AD. The contract for building the tower was signed on 19 August 2011 in the presence of Ivaylo Moskovski, minister of transport, information technology and communications, the BULATSA director general Diyan Dinev, Glavbolgarstroy AD chief executive director Pavel Kalistratov and Glavbolgarstroy AD executive director and management board member Nina Stoyanova signed the design execution and construction contract between BULATSA and Glavbolgarstroy AD for the new control tower at Sofia Airport (Sofia tower).<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Glavbolgartroy AD were selected as contractor, as they were awarded the highest technical rating during the public procurement procedure having proposed the shortest construction timeframe. This project was financed entirely by BULATSA.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lufthansa_Technik-Sofia">Lufthansa Technik-Sofia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Lufthansa Technik-Sofia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9B%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%89%D0%B5_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%84%D0%B8%D1%8F_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/%D0%9B%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%89%D0%B5_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%84%D0%B8%D1%8F_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-%D0%9B%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%89%D0%B5_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%84%D0%B8%D1%8F_-_panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/%D0%9B%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%89%D0%B5_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%84%D0%B8%D1%8F_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-%D0%9B%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%89%D0%B5_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%84%D0%B8%D1%8F_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/%D0%9B%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%89%D0%B5_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%84%D0%B8%D1%8F_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-%D0%9B%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%89%D0%B5_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%84%D0%B8%D1%8F_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9B%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%89%D0%B5_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%84%D0%B8%D1%8F_-_panoramio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lufthansa Technik in Sofia.</div></div></div>\n<p>Lufthansa Technik Sofia was founded in late 2007 as a joint venture between <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Technik" title="Lufthansa Technik">Lufthansa Technik</a> (75.1%) and the Bulgarian Aviation Group (24.9%).<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> With the foundation of Lufthansa Technik Sofia, the Lufthansa Technik Group has created a fifth platform for the overhaul and maintenance of narrowbody aircraft in Europe. The Bulgarian facility serves customers in Europe, the Middle East and North Africa. The facility has undergone a major reconstruction and an upgrade and now can handle the heaviest stage of <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_maintenance_checks" title="Aircraft maintenance checks">aircraft maintenance checks</a>, D-Check, that is now being carried out in Bulgaria. The company have started with more than 350 staff trained in Bulgaria and at Lufthansa Technik facilities in Shannon Base Maintenance operations in the fourth quarter of 2008 with one <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A321" title="Airbus A321">Airbus A321</a> from <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a> as the first customer.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> At the moment the facility in Sofia has more than 1100 employees and plans by the 2018 to hire another 200 employees to reach a total of 1300 employees. The company have completed the building of a new facility in October 2017 which will be used for the maintenance of wide-bodied aircraft and is able to handle <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> With the completion of the new hangar now Lufthansa Technik Sofia has 8 production lines which is turning the Bulgarian unit into the biggest unit of <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Technik" title="Lufthansa Technik">Lufthansa Technik</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rose_Air_Technik">Rose Air Technik</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Rose Air Technik">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 4 July 2018, Rose Air in cooperation with <a href="/wiki/Wizz_Air" title="Wizz Air">Wizz Air</a> opened a new maintenance base at Sofia Airport.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> It is located at the northern part of the airport. The hangar lays on 5000 square meters and has three production lines with overall capacity of 300 planes per year and it can handle C-Check. The base started with more than 100 staff. This will be the first maintenance base for Wizz Air in the Balkans and the fourth in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vrazhdebna_Air_Base"><a href="/wiki/Vrazhdebna_Air_Base" title="Vrazhdebna Air Base">Vrazhdebna Air Base</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Vrazhdebna Air Base">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Vrazhdebna Air Base (also Vrajdebna Air Base) is located at the airport. Operated by the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Air_Force" title="Bulgarian Air Force">Bulgarian Air Force</a>, it is home to the 16th Transport Squadron.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminals">Terminals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Terminals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:100_2904.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/100_2904.JPG/220px-100_2904.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/100_2904.JPG/330px-100_2904.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/100_2904.JPG/440px-100_2904.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2032" data-file-height="1524" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:100_2904.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Inside Terminal 1</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NuevaTerminalAeropuertodeSofia2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/NuevaTerminalAeropuertodeSofia2.jpg/220px-NuevaTerminalAeropuertodeSofia2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/NuevaTerminalAeropuertodeSofia2.jpg/330px-NuevaTerminalAeropuertodeSofia2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/NuevaTerminalAeropuertodeSofia2.jpg/440px-NuevaTerminalAeropuertodeSofia2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NuevaTerminalAeropuertodeSofia2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Interior of Terminal 2</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_1">Terminal 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Terminal 1">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>This terminal was built in the 1930s and opened on 16 September 1937. It has been extended many times, and had a renovation in 2000. Terminal 1 serves low-cost and charter carriers.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_2">Terminal 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Terminal 2">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Terminal 2 was officially opened on 27 December 2006 with the symbolic arrival of <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria_Air" title="Bulgaria Air">Bulgaria Air</a> flight FB 408 from Brussels. It was one of the biggest projects in Bulgaria to receive funds from the EU ISPA programme. The price included the new terminal, new aircraft parking aprons, upgrading the existing aircraft parking aprons and the construction of connecting taxiways. The terminal has seven air-bridges (gates A1, B5\xe2\x80\x939 and C1), 38 check-in desks and covers an area of 50,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (540,000&#160;sq&#160;ft) and has a car park for 820 vehicles. It is located to the east of Terminal 1 and is significantly bigger than the old one which continues to serve low-cost and charter airlines. From 16 January 2017 on Terminal 2 currently serves only one low-cost airline - <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>For the first time in Bulgaria, a terminal has airbridge-equipped gates instead of relying on airside buses.\nAt the eastern end of the Terminal, an end station for Line 1 of the <a href="/wiki/Sofia_Metro" title="Sofia Metro">Sofia Metro</a> has been built under the name <a href="/wiki/Sofia_Airport_Metro_Station" title="Sofia Airport Metro Station">Sofia Airport Metro Station</a>. It was brought into service on 2 April 2015.  The journey between airport and central Sofia takes about 20 minutes with service provided 05.30-24.00 hrs.<sup id="cite_ref-railwaygazette.com_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-railwaygazette.com-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The infrastructure surrounding the building was expected to be completed in 2007. It includes a new dual carriageway road connecting the terminal to the existing airport road, and landscaping including an artificial lake and a fountain. Terminal 2 is designed with special attention to disabled passengers. Their access to the different terminal levels and the <a href="/wiki/Multi-storey_car_park" class="mw-redirect" title="Multi-storey car park">multi-storey car park</a> is facilitated via lifts and escalators.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_facilities">Other facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Other facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Very_Important_Person" class="mw-redirect" title="Very Important Person">VIP</a> terminal is located in the western wing of Terminal 1 and has an entrance of its own, providing an access to four separate rooms \xe2\x80\x93 one main room and two separated rooms with about 20 seats each.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Government terminal is located in the western side of Sofia Airport. The terminal is operated by the <a href="/wiki/28th_Air_Detachment" class="mw-redirect" title="28th Air Detachment">28th Air Detachment</a> which operates government aircraft and operations involving the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Bulgaria" title="President of Bulgaria">President</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Bulgaria" title="Prime Minister of Bulgaria">Prime Minister</a> and other high-ranking government officials.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">Airlines and destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Airlines and destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In 1937 Sofia was used on a route from Berlin to Athens.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> and by 1938 regular direct flights linked Sofia to Belgrade<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Just before the end of the one-party socialist state at the end of the 1980s BALKAN (Bulgarian Airlines) were operating both domestic, and mainly European international routes, to numerous destinations, carrying 2.8m passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The airport is used for scheduled, charter and seasonal operations on many European routes and on several further afield.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="font-size:95%"><tbody><tr><th>Airlines</th><th class="unsortable">Destinations</th></tr><tr><td> <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Airlines" title="Aegean Airlines">Aegean Airlines</a> </td><td> <a href="/wiki/Athens_International_Airport" title="Athens International Airport">Athens</a>\n</td></tr><tr><td> <a href="/wiki/Aeroflot" title="Aeroflot">Aeroflot</a> </td><td> <a href="/wiki/Sheremetyevo_International_Airport" title="Sheremetyevo International Airport">Moscow\xe2\x80\x93Sheremetyevo</a>\n</td></tr><tr><td> <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a> </td><td> <b>Seasonal:</b> <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport" title="Charles de Gaulle Airport">Paris\xe2\x80\x93Charles de Gaulle</a>\n</td></tr><tr><td> <a href="/wiki/Air_Serbia" title="Air Serbia">Air Serbia</a> </td><td> <a href="/wiki/Belgrade_Nikola_Tesla_Airport" title="Belgrade Nikola Tesla Airport">Belgrade</a>\n</td></tr><tr><td> <a href="/wiki/ALK_Airlines" title="ALK Airlines">ALK Airlines</a> </td><td> <b>Seasonal charter:</b> <a href="/wiki/Cairo_International_Airport" title="Cairo International Airport">Cairo</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Teztour_37-0" class="reference"><a href="/wiki/File:Sofia_Airport_Metro_Station.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Sofia_Airport_Metro_Station.JPG/220px-Sofia_Airport_Metro_Station.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Sofia_Airport_Metro_Station.JPG/330px-Sofia_Airport_Metro_Station.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Sofia_Airport_Metro_Station.JPG/440px-Sofia_Airport_Metro_Station.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sofia_Airport_Metro_Station.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sofia_Metro" title="Sofia Metro">Sofia Metro</a> trains at <a href="/wiki/Sofia_Airport_Metro_Station" title="Sofia Airport Metro Station">Sofia Airport Metro Station</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Sofia_Airport_Metro_Station" title="Sofia Airport Metro Station">Sofia Airport Metro Station</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Sofia_Metro" title="Sofia Metro">M4 line</a> is situated next to Terminal 2 and provides connections to the city centre.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A free shuttle bus service between Terminal 1 and Terminal 2 runs from 05:00 until 23:00, connecting arriving and departing passengers from Terminal 1 to metro services.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sofia_Metro" title="Sofia Metro">Sofia Metro</a> also provides a fast connection between the airport and <a href="/wiki/Business_Park_Sofia" title="Business Park Sofia">Business Park Sofia</a>, through interchange at <a href="/wiki/Mladost_1_Metro_Station" title="Mladost 1 Metro Station">Mladost 1 Metro Station</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Sofia_Metro" title="Sofia Metro">M1 line</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus">Bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Three bus routes serve the airport. E84 and E184 connect both terminals to <a href="/wiki/Sofia_University" title="Sofia University">Sofia University</a>, with E84 departing from Terminal 2 and calling at Terminal 1 on the way, and E184 doing the loop in reverse, departing Terminal 1 and calling at Terminal 2 on its way to the centre. Bus 384 only serves Terminal 2, connecting it to <a href="/wiki/Tsarigradsko_shose_Metro_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Tsarigradsko shose Metro Station">Tsarigradsko shose Metro Station</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Car">Car</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Car">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Brussels_Boulevard" title="Brussels Boulevard">Brussels Boulevard</a> is the main thoroughfare to Sofia Airport. There is a new, faster road connection built from Terminal 2 to Brussels Boulevard.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Via Brussels Boulevard and <a href="/wiki/Tsarigradsko_shose" title="Tsarigradsko shose">Tsarigradsko shose</a>, Sofia Airport is connected to both the city centre and eastbound destinations via <a href="/wiki/Trakia_motorway" title="Trakia motorway">Trakia motorway</a> (A1) <a href="/wiki/File:Tabliczka_RO_A1.svg" class="image"><img alt="Tabliczka RO A1.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Tabliczka_RO_A1.svg/20px-Tabliczka_RO_A1.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="12" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Tabliczka_RO_A1.svg/30px-Tabliczka_RO_A1.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Tabliczka_RO_A1.svg/40px-Tabliczka_RO_A1.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="210" data-file-height="130" /></a>\n</p><p>From the northern parts of Sofia, Sofia Airport is conveniently accessible via the East Tangent route. Its junction with Botevgradsko Shose provides access to northbound destinations via <a href="/wiki/Hemus_motorway" title="Hemus motorway">Hemus motorway</a> (A2) <a href="/wiki/File:Tabliczka_RO_A2.svg" class="image"><img alt="Tabliczka RO A2.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Tabliczka_RO_A2.svg/20px-Tabliczka_RO_A2.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="12" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Tabliczka_RO_A2.svg/30px-Tabliczka_RO_A2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Tabliczka_RO_A2.svg/40px-Tabliczka_RO_A2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="210" data-file-height="130" /></a><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Connecting to the southern parts of Sofia and Southwestern Bulgaria is the route via Brussels Boulevard and Boulevard Aleksandar Malinov to <a href="/wiki/Sofia_ring_road" class="mw-redirect" title="Sofia ring road">Sofia ring road</a> <a href="/wiki/File:Nat_road_18_BG.svg" class="image"><img alt="Nat road 18 BG.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Nat_road_18_BG.svg/20px-Nat_road_18_BG.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="13" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Nat_road_18_BG.svg/30px-Nat_road_18_BG.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Nat_road_18_BG.svg/40px-Nat_road_18_BG.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="130" /></a> which has an interchange with southbound <a href="/wiki/Struma_motorway" title="Struma motorway">Struma motorway</a> (A3) <a href="/wiki/File:Mw_A3_BG.svg" class="image"><img alt="Mw A3 BG.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Mw_A3_BG.svg/20px-Mw_A3_BG.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="13" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Mw_A3_BG.svg/30px-Mw_A3_BG.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Mw_A3_BG.svg/40px-Mw_A3_BG.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="130" /></a>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Train">Train</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Train">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>A railway station at Iskarsko shose was inaugurated in April 2015, providing faster interchange from the airport to southbound services on the Bulgarian <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_State_Railways" title="Bulgarian State Railways">national railway system</a>. Situated about 2.5&#160;km (2&#160;mi) from Terminal 2, the train station is accessible via a short trip to <a href="/wiki/Iskarsko_shose_Metro_Station" title="Iskarsko shose Metro Station">Iskarsko shose Metro Station</a> which is two stops away from <a href="/wiki/Sofia_Airport_Metro_Station" title="Sofia Airport Metro Station">Sofia Airport Metro Station</a> on the M4 line.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Incidents_and_accidents">Incidents and accidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Incidents and accidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li>On 22 December 1971, a <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan Airlines">Balkan Airlines</a> <a href="/wiki/Ilyushin_Il-18" title="Ilyushin Il-18">Il-18</a> crashed en route to <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>. 28 people on board died.</li>\n<li>On 22 November 1975, a Balkan Bulgarian airlines An-24 crashed short of the runway after take-off in icy conditions. Of the 48 people on board, three were killed.</li>\n<li>On 10 January 1984, a <a href="/wiki/1984_Balkan_Bulgarian_Tupolev_Tu-134_crash" title="1984 Balkan Bulgarian Tupolev Tu-134 crash">Balkan Bulgarian Airlines Tupolev Tu-134</a> crashed on approach in bad weather. All 50 people on board died.</li>\n<li>On 2 August 1988, a <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan Airlines">Balkan Airlines</a> <a href="/wiki/Yakovlev_Yak-40" title="Yakovlev Yak-40">Yak-40</a> crashed in the <a href="/wiki/Iskar_(river)" title="Iskar (river)">Iskar river</a>. There were 28 fatalities among the 37 passengers on board.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sofia_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Bulgaria" title="List of airports in Bulgaria">List of airports in Bulgaria</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_airlines_of_Bulgaria" title="List of airlines of Bulgaria">List of airlines of Bulgaria</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Europe_by_passenger_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="List of the busiest airports in Europe by passenger traffic">List of the busiest airports in Europe by passenger traffic</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_the_Balkans" title="List of the busiest airports in the Balkans">List of the busiest airports in the Balkans</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
